              <span id="reviewTextContainer1196193727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8881371487751734386"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452045677ra/17639120.gif' width='400' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><strong>Ahhh, why can't all young adult dystopias be like this?! </strong>As you may have noticed in my review for <em>Matched</em>, I think YA dystopias are pretty hard to write. <em>The Testing </em>was so often compared to <em>The Hunger Games </em>and <em>Divergent</em> that I couldn't help but draw similarities between them, as I was reading it. <strong>Though the Tests are somewhat similar to Dauntless Initiation and The Hunger Games</strong>, it's wholly unique and it's own. The pace is excellent, Cia is a an awesome protagonist (who <strong>
  <em>isn't</em>
</strong> a Mary Sue), </span>
  <span id="freeText8881371487751734386" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452045677ra/17639120.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>Ahhh, why can't all young adult dystopias be like this?! </strong>As you may have noticed in my review for <em>Matched</em>, I think YA dystopias are pretty hard to write. <em>The Testing </em>was so often compared to <em>The Hunger Games </em>and <em>Divergent</em> that I couldn't help but draw similarities between them, as I was reading it. <strong>Though the Tests are somewhat similar to Dauntless Initiation and The Hunger Games</strong>, it's wholly unique and it's own. The pace is excellent, Cia is a an awesome protagonist (who <strong>
  <em>isn't</em>
</strong> a Mary Sue), the plot is exhilarating, and <strong>dang</strong>, I couldn't put this book down!<br><br>A brutal World War has left America, along with the rest of the world, a desolate, toxic wasteland. Cities were desecrated, and plants, animals, &amp; humans were mutated. Malencia (Cia) Vale wants nothing more than to attend the United Commonwealth University, where she will be able to help rehabilitate her desolate country and home.<br><br>After her graduation, Cia's wish is granted - she is chosen as a candidate for the Testing. If she passes the Tests thrown at her, she will be admitted to the University. The problem? Wrong answers are penalized with death, &amp; less than twenty percent of the candidates make it through...and some will do anything to achieve a spot.<br><br>I am a <strong>
  <em>huge</em>
</strong> fan of any sort of competition to the death. Mwhuahaha.  But seriously, I really like books with that concept. It's no surprise that I loved the Tests and battle-royale-like competitors.<br><br>You know those books *cough*Divergent<em> </em>*cough* that have an intriguing setting, but don't give any detail as to <em>how</em> the society came to be like that? And no, <em>there was a nuclear war and this totalitarian government rose...</em> is not a thorough enough explanation for my liking. In <em>The Testing</em>, we're actually given the background of <strong>how the United Commonwealth was formed </strong>- the nuclear war is described in detail (Asia declared war on the United States, they retaliated, Africa allies with Asia...etc). I'm aware that's probably inaccurate, but you get the picture. What really fascinated me was the struggles the colonies go through trying to cope with the radiated and mutated soil, and the use of technology to develop hybridized vegetation.<br><br>I also loved the ruins of the major cities like Chicago and St. Louis, and the harsh landscape that had overtaken them. The mutated animals and <em>humans</em> were really neat as well, because they weren't the typical <strong>
  <em>zombies (?) </em>
</strong>that are in every YA book, and they only make an appearance two or three times. They reminded me of the mutts from <em>The </em><em>Hunger Games</em>, but that's probably just because their eyes still appear human, even though the rest of them is a mangled, bloody mess.<br><br><strong>The Testing. </strong>I really liked the idea of the Testing, but had two main issues with it: <em>why are so few admitted to the University</em>, &amp; <em>why would you kill off eighty percent of the most intelligent minds in the Commonwealth?</em> <em> </em>The whole <strong>
  <em>end justifies the means</em>
</strong> saying as an infrastructure for dystopian societies has always seemed unrealistic to me. Looking past that, the Tests were well-done. The officials are constantly monitoring every seemingly, insignificant detail and decision you make. Not only is it a very physical test, but a mental one too. You can't show any weakness or fear, but don't want to be seen as a threat, or else you will surely sabotaged or killed.<br><blockquote>
  <br>
  <strong>“I'll have you fixed in no time. Only...” His eyes narrow. “Only what?” I feel the blush heating my cheeks even before I say, “You're going to have to remove your pants for me to do it.”  </strong>
</blockquote><br>This is going to sound really unimportant and stupid (because it is), but I love it when heroines are short! Hahaha. I'm only 5'2, so it's nice when there are characters who can understand what it's like to be small. *Ahem* Moving on...<strong>Cia isn't a special snowflake</strong>; she's an average 16-year-old girl (though, a little more intelligent than most) who grew up in a relatively small colony, with her parents and four brothers. She's curious, clever, resourceful, and I loved her! <strong>Her humanity and trust in others makes her such a likable protagonist.</strong> Unlike most heroines, Cia doesn't spend half the book mooning over some guy, and isn't magically brilliant and beautiful! I also really liked that she takes an interest in mechanical engineering and botany.<br><br><b>Cia's relationship with Tomas was done really</b> <strong>well. </strong>Tomas may be a <em>little </em>cliche, but what the heck, I thought he was awesome. He's so sweet and caring to Cia. I liked how their romance wasn't insta-love, and it manifested over time. It felt realistic and genuine, and wasn't over done. I especially loved how Cia would call him out if he did something stupid. Haha.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438161927ra/15671431.gif" alt="description" width="419" height="232" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sheesh, I love this book (in case that wasn't clear yet). The characters, setting, plot, romance, and execution are all spectacular. I honestly don't know how this book could've been any better. I'd definitely recommend this to anyone who has an interest in dystopias.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8881371487751734386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_624147913" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/624147913" />
    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4277731-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384212540p2/4277731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/624147913?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/4277731-jon">Jon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=dystopia-post-apocalyptic">dystopia-post-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer624147913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5041767998855784449"><a href='http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Seen at my blog, Scott Reads It!</a><br/>I have absolutely zero self control when it comes to dystopian books. I just have this urge to read any dystopian book I can get my hands on and often I end up extremely disappointed. So many authors are trying to capitalize off the success of The Hunger Games and so their books turn out to be very mediocre. The Testing is essentially a wanna-be, it tries so hard to be the next Hunger Games yet it ultimately fails. <br/><br/> The Testing is about a test that will determine </span>
  <span id="freeText5041767998855784449" style="display:none"><a href="http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Seen at my blog, Scott Reads It!</a><br />I have absolutely zero self control when it comes to dystopian books. I just have this urge to read any dystopian book I can get my hands on and often I end up extremely disappointed. So many authors are trying to capitalize off the success of The Hunger Games and so their books turn out to be very mediocre. The Testing is essentially a wanna-be, it tries so hard to be the next Hunger Games yet it ultimately fails. <br /><br /> The Testing is about a test that will determine whether or not you can go to University. This sounds like an awesome idea but it turns out this extreme standardized test has already been done before and way better (ex: Legend). Next up we have a protagonist who is very one dimensional and suffers from lack of development. I was pretty apathetic and didn't care for Cia at all. Next up we have a love interest whose whole demeanor screamed "Peeta impostor" in my mind. Cia and Tomas's relationship was awfully similar to Katniss and Peeta's romance, there is even a moment that reminded me of the cave scene from The Hunger Games. <br /><br /> The problem with The Testing is that it's pretty tedious and at times it felt like a chore. It's not a good sign when all of your homework is done and you're avoiding the book you're reading. The first half of The Testing (or so) is literally dialogue and Cia taking written exams. The dialogue isn't even witty or entertaining, sometimes the reader wasn't even informed what actually was said. There were so many times in The Testing when instead of saying verbatim what the character said, Charbonneau just tells the reader what they were talking about. The dialogue that was in The Testing was pretty basic and was nothing special at all. <br /><br /> The relationships between the characters were extremely underdeveloped and I didn't care for any of the characters. I don't even remember any of the characters' names (except Cia) because they were so bland and unremarkable. I even had to look up what Cia's love interest was named which is very sad! I remember the characters from books that I read years and years ago, yet I couldn't remember the names of the characters from this book. Nothing stood out to me about these characters because they never really caught my attention. <br /><br /> The romance in this book is extremely awkward and badly done. Cia and Tomas's relationship is built on absolutely nothing and they have zero chemistry at all. The fact that they are from the same area and that they are both taking The Testing, doesn't mean that they have to fall in love with each other. I didn't even understand why Cia and Tomas even liked each other because there was no spark between them. I'm not sure why the author included a romance, my guess is to conform with the generic dystopian mold. <br /><br /> The Testing has some shoddy world-building and I had zero idea how The United Commonwealth was formed. The United Commonwealth was a total mystery to me and I feel like I knew nothing about it at all. To tell you the truth, if there was any world building I'm not sure I would have even cared because I was so bored with this book. I wanted to Charbonneau to make me care about the world she created but she never did.<br /><br /> The Testing isn't absolutely terrible, there a few good things about it. The ending of this book is actually executed surprisingly well and I loved the final action sequences. The author set up the sequel in an extremely interesting way but I don't really have any interest in reading the sequel. (I probably won't read it, but I'm not ruling out the possibility that I will read it). The only thing I didn't like about the ending was the extremely obvious setting up of a love triangle; does every book really need a love triangle? I'm getting sick and tired of all these love triangles because most of them are done so poorly. <br /><br /> I'm pretty confident that The Testing will become a popular book and will sell extremely well. The Testing already has received a starred from Publisher's Weekly and so many bloggers are obsessed with this book. I'm in the minority who didn't enjoy this book; maybe I have read way too many dystopian books. I feel like the dystopian genre can no longer surprise me because so many authors like Charbonneau are just recycling concepts that been done a thousand times over. <br /><br />Bottom Line:<br /><b> <i> If you're looking to read a great dystopian book, The Testing is not for you.</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5041767998855784449" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2784389679?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bren" href="/user/show/61659069-bren">Bren</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=trilogys-and-other-series">trilogys-and-other-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=read-and-reviewed">read-and-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=better-or-worse-than-expected">better-or-worse-than-expected</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2784389679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10486581180149523020">“The earth is resilient, but it’s hard to imagine a time when this place will be anything but a terrible reminder of what we as a people can do.” <br/>― Joelle Charbonneau, The Testing<br/><br/>The Testing is another Dystopian book, part of a series, although I have just read the one. I did not enjoy it to much.<br/><br/>In this world, the story revolves around an Elite college, that some kids get into. It is a chance at a gr eat education in a world where daily struggles are to common. But students are vanishing at the</span>
  <span id="freeText10486581180149523020" style="display:none">“The earth is resilient, but it’s hard to imagine a time when this place will be anything but a terrible reminder of what we as a people can do.” <br />― Joelle Charbonneau, The Testing<br /><br />The Testing is another Dystopian book, part of a series, although I have just read the one. I did not enjoy it to much.<br /><br />In this world, the story revolves around an Elite college, that some kids get into. It is a chance at a gr eat education in a world where daily struggles are to common. But students are vanishing at the school. Once one gets in..do they get out?<br /><br />If I am making it seem like a horror novel it is not. This is pure Dystopian and that was one of the issues for me.<br /><br />There was nothing I can say that was inherently wrong with The Testing. My main reason for not really getting into it, is it is to much like other books I have read which seems to be an issue more and more with this type of novel.<br /><br />The testing has an interesting premise but the story delves into Hunger games territory and I’ve already read the whole Hunger games trilogy and didn’t have much of an interest reading such a similar book. It did not strike me as that original a story and the plot kind of left me cold. Again, this book is not bad. But I felt like I'd read this plot one to many times.<br /><br /> I did make it to the end but I did not read the follow up books. I think if you are a fan of Dystopian and don’t mind a book that is so similar to others, you may like it but for me it did not differentiate itself and I was growing tired as the book went on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10486581180149523020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1972359217" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="booksnpenguins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins"><img alt="booksnpenguins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580407796p2/66222749.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1972359217?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="booksnpenguins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="booksnpenguins" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins">booksnpenguins</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=dystopian-and-scifi">dystopian-and-scifi</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1972359217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2588018467730628696"><blockquote>
  <i>All the living want to do is care for the dead. And now they, too, are among the fallen.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/>For those of you who aren't interested in the entire review, here's a recap:<br/><a href='http://it.tinypic.com?ref=25u5yrs' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1537373421ra/26324838.gif' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/>There.<br/>If that's not exhaustive enough for you, lemme give you all the details. <br/>Like I've said in one of my first reading updates, this reads exactly like something randomly picked from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_' title='The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hunger Games</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13335037.Divergent__Divergent___1_' title='Divergent (Divergent, #1) by Veronica Roth' rel='nofollow noopener'>Divergent</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7735333.Matched__Matched___1_' title='Matched (Matched, #1) by Ally Condie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Matched</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9275658.Legend__Legend___1_' title='Legend (Legend, #1) by Marie Lu' rel='nofollow noopener'>Legend</a>or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10507293.The_Selection__The_Selection___1_' title='The Selection (The Selection, #1) by Kiera Cass' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Selection</a>. <br/>It doesn't matter what page or character you pick, it doesn't make much differenc</span>
  <span id="freeText2588018467730628696" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>All the living want to do is care for the dead. And now they, too, are among the fallen.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><br>For those of you who aren't interested in the entire review, here's a recap:<br><a href="http://it.tinypic.com?ref=25u5yrs" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1537373421ra/26324838.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>There.<br>If that's not exhaustive enough for you, lemme give you all the details. <br>Like I've said in one of my first reading updates, this reads exactly like something randomly picked from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13335037.Divergent__Divergent___1_" title="Divergent (Divergent, #1) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Divergent</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7735333.Matched__Matched___1_" title="Matched (Matched, #1) by Ally Condie" rel="nofollow noopener">Matched</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9275658.Legend__Legend___1_" title="Legend (Legend, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a>or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10507293.The_Selection__The_Selection___1_" title="The Selection (The Selection, #1) by Kiera Cass" rel="nofollow noopener">The Selection</a>. <br>It doesn't matter what page or character you pick, it doesn't make much difference because the essence is the exact same. <br>The winning formula is all there, in all its tropey glory: there's strong heroine with family to save, an incredily fucked up society the protagonist will try to fight, a childhood best friend who won't remain only a friend for so long, lots and lots of drama, and a small amount of action that makes sure you don't fall asleep on every turn of the page. <br>You see what I mean here? It's like reading the same book over and over again, only each time it gets less and less entertaining and interesting. <br>Now, if only this one had something....more. It would have been an entirely different story. <br>Instead, it's a story that rides on all the aforementioned books' success's coattails. Maybe it's a bit tamer and less original than its foreruners, and maybe, that's what penalizes it. <br>The writing surely didn't knock me off my feet. The dialogues were basic and, I don't know if it was me or if the whole story was lacking the kind of world-building you sort of need in books like this one, but I still have some serious trouble understanding <i>why</i> and <i>how</i> certain things happened and were the way they were. What the ever loving frack is The United Commonwealth? One day I'll find out. Or maybe not. <br>The plot...well, it had its moment, but I can't exactly say there's much going on. I swear it has nothing to do with the fact that this book is basically a huge minestrone of ya dystopian elements. <br>If you think I only truly enjoyed myself when bad things happened, you'll understand my grief. <br>In short, it gave me basically nothing in terms of emotion and it's not the kind of story you want to rememer. <br>The beginning is dull and exceptionally boring, but it gets slighlty better as you go on. Mind that I said slightly. I had to force myself to continue and it's never a good thing. Controversies? Plot twists? They apparently don't live here. <br>The characters were okay. I don't mind the protagonist. Cia Vale is nice and capable of making her own choices but she's also overall pretty bland, both in the substance and in the appearance. It must be some kind of requirement to overthrow the goverment, being pretty-without-effort and in such critical and hard times.<br>It also wouldn't kill nobody to see a little more diversity in these books, to be honest. Although it's not a problem that concerns The Testing only, I'm still a bit disappointed about it. <br>The romance too felt a little forced and, in my opinion, unneccessary. It's clear as day that it's underdeveloped and pretty much there to serve a fanbase. Plus, Tomas and Cia have incredibly poor chemistry. If you're one of those people who think Peeta and Katniss match like a pirate boot and a pendrive, this is not the kind of pairing you'll be wanting to root for. Less alone read of it. <br>Ironically enough, I really liked the ending. It felt like Charbonneau did a couple extra shots of Powerade and gave in to her wild inner self. If the entire book looked even slightly like those few last pages did, I think I'd have loved this waaaaaaaaay more than I actually did. <br>I highly approve of wild Charboneau and I'd love to see her again.<br>Just to be clear, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13326831.The_Testing__The_Testing___1_" title="The Testing (The Testing, #1) by Joelle Charbonneau" rel="nofollow noopener">The Testing</a> is not a bad book. At all. <br>It just could have been developed better. It wouldn't have hurt if it had a more original touch, as well. <br>I'm not going to continue the series, but that ending made me want to know what happens next, so I'm picking the shortest and easiest way and creeping my way into one of those summary sites.<br>Feel free to hit me with spoilers if you have any :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="2588018467730628696" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jillian Heise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4100422-jillian-heise"><img alt="Jillian Heise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373991295p2/4100422.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/564309625?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jillian Heise" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jillian Heise" href="/user/show/4100422-jillian-heise">Jillian Heise</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4100422-jillian-heise?shelf=yr-2013-reads">yr-2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4100422-jillian-heise?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer564309625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4277705935763179191">Review originally posted on <a href='www.heisereads.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heise Reads & Recommends</a><br/><br/>First Thought: Oh my goodness! SO good! An engrossing, thrilling, intriguing, suspenseful story set in a well-built future world.<br/><br/>I really enjoyed reading THE TESTING. I was engrossed it in from the start. At first, I was a little worried that it would be too reminiscent of THE HUNGER GAMES and DIVERGENT, but as I got into it, I realized that it was completely it's own creation of this world, while maybe feeling like an homage to those great dys</span>
  <span id="freeText4277705935763179191" style="display:none">Review originally posted on <a href="www.heisereads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Heise Reads &amp; Recommends</a><br /><br />First Thought: Oh my goodness! SO good! An engrossing, thrilling, intriguing, suspenseful story set in a well-built future world.<br /><br />I really enjoyed reading THE TESTING. I was engrossed it in from the start. At first, I was a little worried that it would be too reminiscent of THE HUNGER GAMES and DIVERGENT, but as I got into it, I realized that it was completely it's own creation of this world, while maybe feeling like an homage to those great dystopians that have come before it.<br /><br />It was so hard to put THE TESTING down. Joelle Charbonneau wrote a well-paced plot, and once I got to certain parts throughout, it was impossible not to keep reading so that I could find out what would happen and who would survive. I very much liked the main character, Cia, and was pulling for her throughout the book. She is smart, while still being young and sometimes making decisions that made me want to yell at her, but her intelligence and insights are what keep her going. In a game of who can you trust, she learns to really think through all situations, but that doesn't mean she figures all of it out. In a contest of who can make a great leader, it is difficult to know exactly what the officials might be looking for, but staying true to oneself and one's upbringing can always been seen as the right path. Cia's path is not easy, her decisions are not easy, her ability to live with herself after what she has to do to survive will not be easy, but she stays true to herself which is an admirable quality.<br /><br />The world-building was done well in giving the reader enough information when necessary, but also keeping us guessing about some things. The scenes of explanation are smoothly entrenched in what is happening in the story and propel the plot forward, but also give us enough insight into how things might have come to be this way. The overall idea behind The Testing is so smart, and so manipulative, and scary at the same time. I just hope all of the characters that I have come to like will make it through this series.<br /><br />And, yes, there is an element of romance, but in a brutal contest that is set up to kill off candidates who are not worthy, and a system that is set up to make you question the ulterior motives of everyone around you, and in a world in which all may not be as it seems, how can one be sure of anything that happens during The Testing or trust one's own memories? That remains to be seen.<br /><br />Final Thoughts: I'm calling it now - I think this is going to be the next big dystopian series...it will at least fill that hole left behind from the end of the The Hunger Games and the upcoming end of the Divergent series.</span>

<div id="review_3361414131" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3361414131" />
    <a title="Tessa  HC (onceuponabookworm)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/93925350-tessa-hc-onceuponabookworm"><img alt="Tessa  HC (onceuponabookworm)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591556017p2/93925350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3361414131?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tessa  HC (onceuponabookworm)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tessa  HC (onceuponabookworm)" href="/user/show/93925350-tessa-hc-onceuponabookworm">Tessa  HC (onceuponabookworm)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3361414131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13856775182752886832">This gets 3.75 stars. I was kind of unsatisfied with it. <br/><br/>The Testing follows a girl named Malencia 'Cia' Vale who was worked hard all her life to be chosen for The Testing. The Testing is a test (well duh) that the United Commonwealth, the coalition that arose after the Seven Stages War, uses to select a group of twenty people who will get to go to the University, and become future leaders of the country. Cia is delighted to be chosen for it, but she learns that it may have a darker side that is</span>
  <span id="freeText13856775182752886832" style="display:none">This gets 3.75 stars. I was kind of unsatisfied with it. <br /><br />The Testing follows a girl named Malencia 'Cia' Vale who was worked hard all her life to be chosen for The Testing. The Testing is a test (well duh) that the United Commonwealth, the coalition that arose after the Seven Stages War, uses to select a group of twenty people who will get to go to the University, and become future leaders of the country. Cia is delighted to be chosen for it, but she learns that it may have a darker side that is erased from the candidates' memories, and that she shouldn't trust anyone. <br /><br />I think that's as far as I can get without spoiling. Now onto the spoiler filled part of the review. The bottom line is at the bottom if you don't want to be spoiled. <br /><br />First off, Cia breaks rule number one (Don't trust anyone) in the literal first freaking hour of the freaking ride to the capital, Tosu City. She trusts Tomas. She tells him about her father and his nightmares. She tells him basically everything. And that's a whole lot of trust right there. So why did she do it?<br />My theory is that the author used Cia's trusty nature and her immediate trust in Tomas to move forward the romance, which, I have to tell you, is badly written. They're holding hands before anything real even happens in the book. I suppose you could say that the author says they danced at some school dance and made other girls jealous. But that backstory has so little substance that it seems very weird when they're just holding hands. If you didn't know already, I love me a good slow romance that takes a while to set it, maybe one <b>(1)</b> kiss in the first book, a couple of kisses in the second, and more in the third (if it's a trilogy). That is my idea of a well-written romance. It makes you want the characters to get together more than anything. As in, <b>not this book</b>. And declarations of love in the <i>first book</i> of a trilogy just pissed me off. I mean, really? Rushing much? I hated how they were holding hands in the first half of the book. I mean, author, make us want the romance before serving it to us on a silver platter! I didn't want, nor liked, the romance in this book. <br />That's not the entire reason why I didn't like this book all that much. Don't get me wrong, it was a really good book, which made me terrified at some parts, shocked at others, and wanting to read more and more, but it did have its flaws. For example, in the beginning what was annoying was that every sentence seemed to have a justification after it. If it brought in a new idea, it would justify it when it didn't need justifying. For example, (this didn't happen in the book, it's just the first thing I could think of) <i>There were apples in the buffet. There were green and red apples</i>. I mean, we get that there are apples, and we know that there are different kinds of apples, so one would assume that there would be green and red apples. By the way, if you didn't pick this up already, this <b>was not in the book</b>. Don't come yelling at me later. It's just an example I made up. But you get the idea. <br />Another thing that annoyed me was that Cia seemed to know how to do everything, and passed most of the book with minor problems. Her father taught her science, from what I picked up, and she knows plants well enough, and she's smart. Okay. But during the test with the wires, how did she know how to do everything right without problems? I don't believe that it was sheer luck that got her through that test. And she just knew to check the other guy's booklet with the questions in the third test. I mean, wasn't that all too convenient. Tomas gets impaled in the butt? Goody, she knows how to burn away flesh! They're chased by a pack of mutated wolves? Somehow Cia and Tomas can run away faster with their bikes. Her bike breaks? She somehow has all the tools, (wires, screws, and bolts, from page 283) to fashion a new bike that will hold her and Tomas. I mean, did I fall asleep during the part that explained where she got those tools from? Probably. And did her water purification tablets and pain relieving medicine never run out? Did she have an endless supply? I would like to know. <br />I was kind of disappointed in the ending, because Cia forgot everything, obviously, but I felt it could have been done better. I was instantly intrigued at the part from Zeen's point of view. I would like to continue the series, but that may take a while. <br /><br /><b>Bottom line:</b> This book has a really good story, which I'm sure you'll like, if you have the patience. Or if you don't have a tendency to see all the flaws in a book. Both ways, I'd recommend giving this a try! </span>
  <a data-text-id="13856775182752886832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_888254325" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/888254325" />
    <a title="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3854740-christina-ensconced-in-lit"><img alt="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372018610p2/3854740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/888254325?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" href="/user/show/3854740-christina-ensconced-in-lit">Christina (Ensconced in Lit)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer888254325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13414673211205150712">I won this ARC from a blog giveaway, thanks! This has probably been my favorite read in the past few weeks, but I couldn't give it five stars for issues that I couldn't ignore.<br/><br/>The Testing by Joelle Charbonneau has been on my list to read for a long time. It's been compared to the Hunger Games, and stars Cia, who is in one of the colonies who have not had any candidates selected for The Testing in a long time. The Testing has been put in place after war has devastated the world to find the best c</span>
  <span id="freeText13414673211205150712" style="display:none">I won this ARC from a blog giveaway, thanks! This has probably been my favorite read in the past few weeks, but I couldn't give it five stars for issues that I couldn't ignore.<br /><br />The Testing by Joelle Charbonneau has been on my list to read for a long time. It's been compared to the Hunger Games, and stars Cia, who is in one of the colonies who have not had any candidates selected for The Testing in a long time. The Testing has been put in place after war has devastated the world to find the best candidate leaders of the country to go to University. No one in Cia's town knows much about The Testing except for her own father, who refuses to speak about it. Cia is chosen with three other people in her class, and she starts a difficult and treacherous journey where either death or glory can await. <br /><br />I admit I was really into this book. Cia is a great main character-- she's humble, gracious, and has a good heart. But at the same time, she is super intelligent and has obviously been trained well by both her school and her father. Other reviewers have mentioned that she may be too perfect, at least in the sense of being able to do things and always being right for the most part, at least about her instincts on traps and puzzles. I agree. It would have been nice to see other characters contribute as well. They obviously were smart enough to get there.<br /><br />Some reviewers were upset with how "boring" the testing part was, but actually, I loved that part. I really enjoyed the section where Cia figures out something key that allows her to pass to the next test and thought it was pretty clever. The test revealed something about several of the characters. I did think it was odd that even though her father gave her the warning not to trust anyone, she seems to have developed a sixth sense suspicion, which seems almost too good to be true. I also liked the descriptions of the other tests. It shows what kinds of things Cia is good at before she gets tested further in the third portion of the test.<br /><br />The journey Cia takes with her love interest, Tomas, from thereon out was gripping, and I wanted to know what each of the characters were hiding. I was definitely surprised by some of the outcomes. This was the first book in a while that I was contemplating buying the next book on Kindle immediately to see what happens next.<br /><br />That said, other than the issues I alluded to above, there were a couple of other problems. I agree with others that the love connection between Cia and Tomas seems kind of quick and unbelievable. There are "hints" to the past, about looking longingly at each other during a dance, but we never see that, so we never really feel for them and root for them. And lastly, the world building isn't perfect. I definitely don't get why people have to die during the Testing. And what happens to the people who fail? It isn't clear what happens to them-- but I feel like the book hints to them being executed. It seems to me that people that put their own gain above the needs for others (meaning people who kill to "win") would probably not make very good leaders, but hey, that's me. Hopefully, more world building will be revealed in the next book.<br /><br />Overall, there are definite similarities between this book and The Hunger Games, and probably has been in somewhat inspired by that trilogy, but I believe it stands on its own. I don't know if it's because I haven't read a dystopian in a while (I burned myself out like many other reviewers and then took a long break), or what, but I really like the "test" aspect to the whole thing, which was definitely lacking in The Hunger Games, which it should, since that wasn't the focus. <br /><br />I think this was a great debut novel, and Charbonneau definitely has a talent at keeping us on our toes and glued to the page. Even though I have 20 more books to get through, I may just take a break from my reading list and pick up the second today.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13414673211205150712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1080861704" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1080861704" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1080861704?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781470326210" href="/book/show/20660097-the-testing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1080861704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13881500956657244861">What shall I say here????? I've seen the comparisons between this book and <i>Hunger Games</i>. I suppose that can't be escaped. YA novels tend to run in cycles. After harry Potter dozens of books placed in "magical schools" hit the shelves. Some were good, others not so much.<br/><br/>Now that said...there's actually very little resemblance between this book and <i>Hunger Games</i> other than there is a part of the plot where a group of young people are in a situation where they can end up trying to kill each other.<br/><br/>He</span>
  <span id="freeText13881500956657244861" style="display:none">What shall I say here????? I've seen the comparisons between this book and <i>Hunger Games</i>. I suppose that can't be escaped. YA novels tend to run in cycles. After harry Potter dozens of books placed in "magical schools" hit the shelves. Some were good, others not so much.<br /><br />Now that said...there's actually very little resemblance between this book and <i>Hunger Games</i> other than there is a part of the plot where a group of young people are in a situation where they can end up trying to kill each other.<br /><br />Here we have (another) post-apocalyptic world. The population is busily involved in trying to repair the world...repair the damage done in the "7 Stages of War". The population was left decimated (That's not to be taken literally, I actually think more than one in ten were killed) and society has pretty much had to be rebuilt from scratch. We're in North America and people are now living in colonies. The colonies are places where new populations are working on the said restoration.<br /><br />"And" each year the best and brightest are pulled from each colony for a "chance" to get one of twenty slots at..."The University".<br /><br />Of course when over a hundred candidates show up you need to reduce that pool of possible University students somehow...<br /><br />I like the book. I've been thinking over my rating. I'd say the 4 star rating may not be my "tippity tip top" 4 but it's an enthusiastic one.<br /><br />The book is good, the story is interesting (though with a few internal flaws, mostly in logic) and it does hold the interest. There's a fairly predictable but well handled secret that is part of the logical inconsistency of the story <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[with something north of 70 young people vanishing every year, even if all University Grads are sent to "different colonies" than the one from which they originated I'd think eventually the colonies at large might "smell a rat".  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> with our young hero being sent off to have a chance at University (her life long dream) along with 4 other of her classmates for "Testing" to see who get's one of the University slots, we're off.<br /><br />I found the book to be fairly interesting from the opening lines and very interesting from the time the testing begins. I think readers will spot things before the "candidates" but that's only because "we" will go into the book looking for something.<br /><br />There's one other glaring logical problem with this plot, but the main character notices it herself so I assume it is something the author plans to address in a future volume. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ if the population is that small and they are trying to rebuild then why kill off dozens of the best and brightest every year???? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Anyway...as noted, I like the book and recommend the book. Enjoy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13881500956657244861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_585230101" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/585230101" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/585230101?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=blue">blue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=survival">survival</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=arc-netgalley">arc-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=babr-reviews">babr-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=zzread-april-2013">zzread-april-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer585230101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1309797304252970820"><b>Update 12/4/13</b> This book is free on <a href='http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B008LQ1VGC/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=B008LQ1VGC&linkCode=as2&tag=bookwdream-20' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> today. <br/><br/><b>Initial thoughts:</b> 3.5-4.0 stars. Despite my reservations, I did enjoy this book and while there are parallels to <b>The Hunger Games</b> (2nd half of the book), it is a solid start to the series. I'll definitely be reading on. <br/><br/><b>My review:</b><br/><b>The Testing</b> takes place in a world ravaged by the aftermath of war and a series of natural disasters. Resources are limited: a university education is a highly coveted prize. Each year a group of the most talented studen</span>
  <span id="freeText1309797304252970820" style="display:none"><b>Update 12/4/13</b> This book is free on <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B008LQ1VGC/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=B008LQ1VGC&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=bookwdream-20" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> today. <br /><br /><b>Initial thoughts:</b> 3.5-4.0 stars. Despite my reservations, I did enjoy this book and while there are parallels to <b>The Hunger Games</b> (2nd half of the book), it is a solid start to the series. I'll definitely be reading on. <br /><br /><b>My review:</b><br /><b>The Testing</b> takes place in a world ravaged by the aftermath of war and a series of natural disasters. Resources are limited: a university education is a highly coveted prize. Each year a group of the most talented students are chosen to compete in The Testing for one of the twenty available spots. The competition is ruthless and many candidates succumb to the pressure. Others are not so lucky: their mistakes carry a higher cost – their lives. <br /><br />Cia Vale is from the Five Lakes Colony. When she and four others from her small town are chosen to compete in The Testing, she is very excited. Her family does not share her enthusiasm. Her father had been through The Testing years ago and he does not have any memories of the selection process. Cia, along with her friends, is taken by skimmer to the capital city of Tosu where they will be tested. <br /><br />At first the tests seem innocuous: general knowledge exams in which Cia and her friends from Five Lakes Colony do well. As the testing progresses, a more sinister side becomes apparent. The competition becomes more brutal. Failure to complete a test correctly can results in pain or dismemberment or even death. <br /><br />Then comes phase two. This is where the candidates are dropped off into the wilderness and told to find a way back to Tosu. This is where the book becomes very “Hunger Games-ish.” Cia and Tomas vow to work together to find their way back. <br /><br />I think that I really enjoyed the second half of the book. The pacing was action packed and you never really knew what obstacle would be thrown in Cia and Tomas’ way. I adored Cia and Tomas The romance between these two was tender and sweet. I loved how they took care of each other. Cia and Tomas are the MacGyvers of this world. Give Cia a box of nuts and bolts and other assorted junk and that girl will fashion a bicycle. Cia was so smart and resourceful. I also liked that she had strong morals and did not resort to the dirty tricks that the other candidates used. <br /><br />As I read this book, I couldn’t help but think why a society would have only twenty spots for a university education. Surely a society ravaged by war and all sorts of environmental disasters would want to keep all of its most promising students and leadership candidates rather than killing them off in some ridiculous testing program. This is the part where I just had to suspend belief and just keep reading. <br /><br /><b>The Testing</b> is a solid start to the series. The next book <b>The Testing: Independent Study </b>is expected to be published January 7, 2014. If you’d like to get a sample of this author’s writing, there is a free prequel available called <b>The Testing Guide</b>. This short story gives an overview of the world and also includes the first 3 chapters of <b>The Testing</b>. <br /><br /><i>Thank you to NetGalley and Houghton Mifflin Harcourt for a review copy of this book. </i><br /><br /><b>Review posted on <a href="http://badassbookreviews.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Badass Book Reviews.</a></b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1309797304252970820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer584869575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9388033162609453525"><b>Thank you NetGalley for providing me with an ARC of this book!</b><br/><br/><b>Actual rating: 2.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Most of the world has become a wasteland, and is in need of a new generation of leaders to piece society back together. But in order to become part of this group of future leaders, a select few teens are required to pass the Testing. <br/><br/>Cia Vale is thrilled when she is selected as a candidate. But before she leaves, her father––a former participant of the Testing––gives her an ominous warning, hinting that there i</span>
  <span id="freeText9388033162609453525" style="display:none"><b>Thank you NetGalley for providing me with an ARC of this book!</b><br /><br /><b>Actual rating: 2.5 stars</b><br /><br />Most of the world has become a wasteland, and is in need of a new generation of leaders to piece society back together. But in order to become part of this group of future leaders, a select few teens are required to pass the Testing. <br /><br />Cia Vale is thrilled when she is selected as a candidate. But before she leaves, her father––a former participant of the Testing––gives her an ominous warning, hinting that there is a very dark side to the test she is about to take. Above all, he makes one thing clear: she can't trust anyone.<br /><br />When the Testing begins, Cia discovers that her father was right. It's every man for himself, and it soon becomes clear that the other candidates are willing to stab each other in the back in order to pass. … And failing has more dire consequences than Cia anticipated. <br /><br />Over all, this book was very "meh" for me. It wasn't terrible, but there wasn't much to distinguish it from other YA dystopian books. It seemed like it was just borrowing elements from other dystopian books and didn't have much to offer in terms of originality. (I mean, just look at it … even the cover is a pretty blatant rip-off of the Hunger Games covers; same with the chapter headings.)<br /><br />I found the first half of the book pretty dull. It mostly consists of a bunch of kids sitting around taking tests (like, you know, pencil and paper tests). It gradually builds up to more threatening tests, in which a person or two dies a horrible death for giving a wrong answer or making a wrong move, etc. But … it's still kind of like "extreme SATs" or something. <br /><br />The pace doesn't pick up until about halfway through the book, in which the final test consists of the characters being dropped off in a random place, and they have to find their way back to the starting point. (And they're allowed to kill each other along the way, of course.) But even with the rise in action, the second half of the book is pretty repetitive and I didn't find it too engaging.<br /><br />Cia is not a very strong protagonist, either, and she's pretty much a Mary Sue. She's super smart, and she tends to antagonize all the other characters and make them sound like inhuman, unfeeling beings. She has kind of a "everyone is a shallow jerk except for me" attitude. <br /><br />The rest of the characters weren't very interesting or relatable to me, either. They were all pretty bland and didn't have very strong motives or personalities. <br /><br />There's also a romance, but it's not very well-developed or believable. It felt forced to me. <br /><br />Also, the writing is pretty "telling" rather than showing. There's a lot of plot summary, and the author tends to skim over dialogue by writing things like, "First we talked about this thing, then we talked about another thing. Then we talked about the other thing some more." It's like … I don't want to just hear what you talked about, I want to know <i>what the characters actually said</i>. Skipping over the dialogue like that is boring, and it also detracts from the character development. <br /><br />I think there are some interesting themes in the book, and some interesting social/political messages about what it takes to be a leader––whether leaders should be ruthless or compassionate, and so on. And the story did have its exciting bits.<br /><br />But, ultimately, it just didn't completely hold my attention and it wasn't original enough to be very memorable for me, and it wasn't enough for me to want to continue the series. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9388033162609453525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer507414868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15867559448719835985"><i>I received an ARC copy of this book from the publishers via Netgalley.</i><br/><br/>Reading this book you can't help but compare it the The Hunger Games. It's inevitable. But as I read this book and turned each page, one thought came to mind: This is way more awesome then The Hunger Games can ever be! Yes, you read that right. This is way better and so much more awesome then Suzanne Collins' series. Why? I'll tell you why without giving away any spoilers!<br/><br/>Although this story resembles THG, it's different in a </span>
  <span id="freeText15867559448719835985" style="display:none"><i>I received an ARC copy of this book from the publishers via Netgalley.</i><br /><br />Reading this book you can't help but compare it the The Hunger Games. It's inevitable. But as I read this book and turned each page, one thought came to mind: This is way more awesome then The Hunger Games can ever be! Yes, you read that right. This is way better and so much more awesome then Suzanne Collins' series. Why? I'll tell you why without giving away any spoilers!<br /><br />Although this story resembles THG, it's different in a lot of ways. First of all, the story Joelle worked out is so much better and more detailed then THG. I was so fascinated reading this book. You get a lot of detailed of what happens in the past and I liked that a lot. Especially since it never got boring. The writing is so so good. It holds my attention and I couldn't put it down. The questions you have only build up and you rarely get an answer. I still have a lot of questions left unanswered. And that's good. It makes me want to read the second book even more. It makes me curious as hell. The writing is so good I could feel the tension between the lines. Seriously, not much authors can do that.<br /><br />So what is this story about, really? Well, apparently all hell broke loose in the past. Literally. The world is destroyed and rebuild. That's the world Cia lives in. After she's been chosen for The Testing, her father warns her not to trust anyone. And Cia is smart. She prepares for the worst. Her brothers learned her how to defend herself and she never forgets where she came from throughout the story. She is a caring and loving girl that always wants to help others and she is strong. Maybe not physical, but mentally for sure. That helps her a lot. She isn't perfect though. She trust people to easily despite her father's warning. <br />So when she arrives in at the Testing center, she is prepared for the worst to happen. In the beginning everything seems okay. But then the weird and sinister stuff happens that makes you, as a reader, question what the goal of the leaders of the city, the United Commonwealth, really is. It really freaked me out at times. Nothing is what is seems. <br /><br />I know I only talked about the Main Character, but I can't talk about the other ones without giving away spoilers. So I'll leave you with a tip. Do what Cia's father said: <b> TRUST NO ONE.</b></span>

<div id="review_2414990110" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2414990110" />
    <a title="Bookish Penguin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54202999-bookish-penguin"><img alt="Bookish Penguin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572470988p2/54202999.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2414990110?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookish Penguin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookish Penguin" href="/user/show/54202999-bookish-penguin">Bookish Penguin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781848776531" href="/book/show/17711954-the-testing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54202999-bookish-penguin?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2414990110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1819756971914038301">I am really torn between how to rate this book and what to write now because I really really enjoyed this book but then I read other reviews...reviews of readers who rated the book with 3 stars or lower because I always like having different POVs on a book I read. So yeah they kind of opened my eyes to see the flaws of "The Testing" and I really didn't want to see them since I liked it so much. I know everyone should always make up an own opinion but you also can't just close your eyes and prete</span>
  <span id="freeText1819756971914038301" style="display:none">I am really torn between how to rate this book and what to write now because I really really enjoyed this book but then I read other reviews...reviews of readers who rated the book with 3 stars or lower because I always like having different POVs on a book I read. So yeah they kind of opened my eyes to see the flaws of "The Testing" and I really didn't want to see them since I liked it so much. I know everyone should always make up an own opinion but you also can't just close your eyes and pretend flaws aren't there.<br /><br />I don't know what to say. I personally enjoyed this book and flew through it. I am a fool for dystopian books. The plot was good and I was with the characters, mostly with Cia all the time. The idea was good and so was the writing. I will read further because I'd like to know whats going to happen and they seem like easy yet not boring reads.<br /><br />But what about the bad reviews? Some of their key-points below:<br /><br />-<b>Copy from Panem:</b>Well I guess everyone says this about every dystopian book where one needs to fight for survival. But I see it. I see it is like Panem.<br /><br />-<b>Copying exact scences:</b> Before reading reviews I didn't have this feeling. But yeah human like creatures with the eyes of said humans and the chasing..Yes it is copied.<br /><br />-<b>The writing being dull and distant:</b> I did not recognized this either. Yet all those people saying it are right. It is distant. We don't get good conversations or noone at all and just descriptions of them.<br /><br />-<b>Killing their best people might not be a good idea:</b> Well yes it sure isn't. What were those guys even thinking?? I get the point of killing them if they doubt the system. But just becauser they failed a math test or got their wounds healed? This seems dumb. I thought they would do everything to save man kind since there are not many left.<br /><br />There are more points but I don't wanna list anything anymore... I really just want to enjoy the other two books without thinking of all the other stuff may it be Panem or else.<br /><br />This is not a new Panem. Nothing is going to be a new Panem since Panem is always in my heart and I have watched the first movie 20 times now and this number is going to extend. I like reading the books. It's like coming home.<br />But we can't always compare books. <br /><br />(Yet I know if I had read it later or early I might have hated it. Who knows. Who cares? I enjoyed it the time I read it and this counts.)<br /><br />Everything is going to be copied eventually.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1819756971914038301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('X5JubMnUjCX1TnOOYDCoxkx9M/Li4KP9wpr119YnQKoYBF2kmm8b1uT0BqkayD+HpExukrkX7p2XCn074rm6FQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('t0eAhUaDiPrxgQ1zWAbv3YxsyZFbcMnMvQGJJRfZciPw0bNNFTgfCeA7eFQi/nicZF2U8QCHhKzokQHJI0eInA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer10670128465341745003">I am a storyteller at heart. I have performed in a variety of operas, musical theatre and children's theatre productions across the Chicagoland area. <br/><br/>While I'm happy to perform for an audience, I am equally delighted to teach private voice lessons and use my experience from the stage to create compelling characters on the page.   <span id="freeText10670128465341745003" style="display:none">I am a storyteller at heart. I have performed in a variety of operas, musical theatre and children's theatre productions across the Chicagoland area. <br /><br />While I'm happy to perform for an audience, I am equally delighted to teach private voice lessons and use my experience from the stage to create compelling characters on the page. I am the author of the Rebecca Robbins mystery series (Minotaur Books), The Paige Marshall Glee Club mysteries (Berkley) and The Testing YA triology (Houghton Mifflin Harcourt).<br /><br /></span>
